Tim Lenz, John Anderson, and I visited --&gt; Lemmon Valley Marsh on a hot Sunday afternoon (30 July --&gt; 2000).  Lemmon Valley Marsh is just north of Reno, in --&gt; Washoe County.  Our quest was shorebirds, of which we --&gt; found a few, as follows: --&gt; --&gt; 1. Killdeer               200 --&gt; 2. American Avocet         80 --&gt; 3. Black-necked Stilt     390 --&gt; 4. Willet                   1 --&gt; 5. Marbled Godwit           1 --&gt; 6. Long-billed Dowitcher    6 --&gt; 7. Wilson's Phalarope      10 --&gt; 8. Red-necked Phalarope    20 --&gt;    phalarope, sp.          40 --&gt; --&gt; Other birds observed included: large numbers of White-faced --&gt; Ibises; good numbers and variety of dabbling ducks (including --&gt; a Ruddy Duck who looked like he had just dipped his bill in --&gt; a bucket of blue paint); a calling Sora; lots of California --&gt; Gulls and a few Ring-billed Gulls; a truly bedraggled-looking --&gt; largish gull that we couldn't identify, but which looked --&gt; interesting; and a few Bank Swallows (yesterday Tim saw about --&gt; 20 at this site). --&gt; --&gt; Large numbers of birds are using Lemmon Valley Marsh now, --&gt; and seekers of rarities should definitely be checking those --&gt; ibis, duck, and gull flocks for rarities wandering northward --&gt; from their breeding grounds!	Lemmon Valley Marsh, w Tim Lenz, Ted Floyd
